   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Film industry
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:264px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Film_Crew.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1513" data-file-width="1860" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Film_Crew.jpg/262px-Film_Crew.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Film_Crew.jpg/393px-Film_Crew.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Film_Crew.jpg/524px-Film_Crew.jpg 2x" width="262"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Film_Crew.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Film_crew" title="Film crew">
          Film crew
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        film industry
       </b>
       or
       <b>
        motion picture industry
       </b>
       comprises the technological and commercial institutions of
       <a href="/wiki/Filmmaking" title="Filmmaking">
        filmmaking
       </a>
       , i.e., film
       <a href="/wiki/Production_company" title="Production company">
        production companies
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Movie_studio" title="Movie studio">
        film studios
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cinematography" title="Cinematography">
        cinematography
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Animation" title="Animation">
        animation
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Film_production" title="Film production">
        film production
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Screenwriting" title="Screenwriting">
        screenwriting
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pre-production" title="Pre-production">
        pre-production
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post_production" title="Post production">
        post production
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Film_festival" title="Film festival">
        film festivals
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Distribution_(business)" title="Distribution (business)">
        distribution
       </a>
       ; and
       <a href="/wiki/Actor" title="Actor">
        actors
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Film_director" title="Film director">
        film directors
       </a>
       , and other
       <a href="/wiki/Film_crew" title="Film crew">
        film crew
       </a>
       personnel.
      </p>
      <p>
       Though the expense involved in making
       <a href="/wiki/Film" title="Film">
        films
       </a>
       almost immediately led film production to concentrate under the auspices of standing production companies, advances in affordable film making equipment, and expansion of opportunities to acquire investment capital from outside the film industry itself, have allowed
       <a href="/wiki/Independent_film" title="Independent film">
        independent film
       </a>
       production to evolve.
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_States" title="Cinema of the United States">
        Hollywood
       </a>
       is the oldest film industry of the world,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the largest in terms of box office gross revenue.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_cinema" title="Indian cinema">
        Indian cinema
       </a>
       (including
       <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">
        Bollywood
       </a>
       ) is the largest film industry in terms of the number of films produced and the number of tickets sold, with 3.5 billion tickets sold annually (compared to Hollywood's 2.6 billion tickets sold annually)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and 1,986 feature films produced annually.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-filmfed_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-filmfed-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_film_industry">
        Modern film industry
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Modern film industry">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="vertical-navbox nowraplinks" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em 0;text-align:center;line-height:1.4em;font-size:88%">
       <tr>
        <th class="navbox-abovebelow" style="padding:0.1em">
         <a href="/wiki/World_cinema" title="World cinema">
          World cinema
         </a>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em;text-align:left;">
         <div>
          <ul>
           <li>
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_cinema" title="African cinema">
             African cinema
            </a>
           </li>
           <li>
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_cinema" title="Asian cinema">
             Asian cinema
            </a>
           </li>
          </ul>
          <dl>
           <dd>
            <small>
             <a href="/wiki/East_Asian_cinema" title="East Asian cinema">
              East Asian cinema
             </a>
             <br/>
             <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_cinema" title="South Asian cinema">
              South Asian cinema
             </a>
             <br/>
             <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asian_cinema" title="Southeast Asian cinema">
              Southeast Asian cinema
             </a>
             <br/>
             <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Asian_cinema" title="West Asian cinema">
              West Asian cinema
             </a>
            </small>
           </dd>
          </dl>
          <ul>
           <li>
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_cinema" title="European cinema">
             European cinema
            </a>
           </li>
           <li>
            <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_cinema" title="Latin American cinema">
             Latin American cinema
            </a>
           </li>
           <li>
            <a href="/wiki/North_American_cinema" title="North American cinema">
             North American cinema
            </a>
           </li>
           <li>
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oceanian_cinema" title="Oceanian cinema">
             Oceanian cinema
            </a>
           </li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The worldwide theatrical market had a box office of
       <span style="white-space: nowrap">
        US$38.6 billion
       </span>
       in 2016. The top three continents/regions by box office gross were: Asia-Pacific with
       <span style="white-space: nowrap">
        US$14.9 billion
       </span>
       , the U.S. and Canada with
       <span style="white-space: nowrap">
        US$11.4 billion
       </span>
       , and Europe, the Middle East and North Africa with
       <span style="white-space: nowrap">
        US$9.5 billion
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of 2016, the largest markets by box office were, in decreasing order, the United States, China, Japan, India, and the United Kingdom. As of 2011, the countries with the largest number of film productions were India, Nigeria, and the United States. In Europe, significant centers of movie production are France, Germany, Italy, Spain, and the United Kingdom.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUROAVCOUNCIL-20090511_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-EUROAVCOUNCIL-20090511-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Distinct from the centers are the locations where movies are filmed. Because of labor and infrastructure costs, many films are produced in countries other than the one in which the company which pays for the film is located. For example, many U.S. movies are filmed in Canada, many Nigerian movies are filmed in
       <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">
        Ghana
       </a>
       , while many Indian movies are filmed in the Americas, Europe,
       <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">
        Singapore
       </a>
       etc.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="China">
        China
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: China">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_China" title="Cinema of China">
        Cinema of China
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Qufu_Cinema_-_P1060026.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Qufu_Cinema_-_P1060026.JPG/220px-Qufu_Cinema_-_P1060026.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Qufu_Cinema_-_P1060026.JPG/330px-Qufu_Cinema_-_P1060026.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Qufu_Cinema_-_P1060026.JPG/440px-Qufu_Cinema_-_P1060026.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Qufu_Cinema_-_P1060026.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Old Chinese Cinema in
         <a href="/wiki/Qufu" title="Qufu">
          Qufu
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Shandong" title="Shandong">
          Shandong
         </a>
         , China
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Cinema of China
       </b>
       is one of three distinct historical threads of
       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">
        Chinese-language
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Film" title="Film">
        cinema
       </a>
       together with the
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Hong_Kong" title="Cinema of Hong Kong">
        cinema of Hong Kong
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Taiwan" title="Cinema of Taiwan">
        cinema of Taiwan
       </a>
       . Cinema was introduced in China in 1896 and the first Chinese film,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Battle_of_Dingjunshan_(film)" title="The Battle of Dingjunshan (film)">
         The Battle of Dingjunshan
        </a>
       </i>
       , was made in 1905, with the film industry being centered on
       <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">
        Shanghai
       </a>
       in the first decades. China is the home of the largest film studio in the world, the
       <a href="/wiki/Hengdian_World_Studios" title="Hengdian World Studios">
        Hengdian World Studios
       </a>
       , and in 2010 it had the third largest film industry by number of feature films produced annually. For the next decade the production companies were mainly foreign-owned, and the domestic film industry was centered on Shanghai, a thriving
       <a href="/wiki/Entrep%C3%B4t" title="Entrepôt">
        entrepot
       </a>
       and the largest city in the
       <a href="/wiki/Far_East" title="Far East">
        Far East
       </a>
       . In 1913, the first independent Chinese
       <a href="/wiki/Screenplay" title="Screenplay">
        screenplay
       </a>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Difficult_Couple" title="The Difficult Couple">
         The Difficult Couple
        </a>
       </i>
       , was filmed in
       <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">
        Shanghai
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Zheng_Zhengqiu" title="Zheng Zhengqiu">
        Zheng Zhengqiu
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Shichuan" title="Zhang Shichuan">
        Zhang Shichuan
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As the Sixth Generation gained international exposure, many subsequent movies were joint ventures and projects with international backers, but remained quite resolutely low-key and low budget. Jia's
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Platform_(2000_film)" title="Platform (2000 film)">
         Platform
        </a>
       </i>
       (2000) was funded in part by
       <a href="/wiki/Takeshi_Kitano" title="Takeshi Kitano">
        Takeshi Kitano
       </a>
       's production house,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:1-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       while his
       <i>
        Still Life
       </i>
       was shot on HD video.
       <i>
        Still Life
       </i>
       was a surprise addition and
       <a href="/wiki/Golden_Lion" title="Golden Lion">
        Golden Lion
       </a>
       winner of the 2006 Venice International Film Festival.
       <i>
        Still Life
       </i>
       , which concerns provincial workers around the
       <a href="/wiki/Three_Gorges" title="Three Gorges">
        Three Gorges
       </a>
       region, sharply contrasts with the works of Fifth
       <a href="/wiki/Generation" title="Generation">
        Generation
       </a>
       Chinese directors like
       <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Yimou" title="Zhang Yimou">
        Zhang Yimou
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Chen_Kaige" title="Chen Kaige">
        Chen Kaige
       </a>
       who were at the time producing
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/House_of_Flying_Daggers" title="House of Flying Daggers">
         House of Flying Daggers
        </a>
       </i>
       (2004) and
       <i>
        The Promise
       </i>
       (2005). It featured no star of international renown and was acted mostly by non-professionals. In 2012 the country became the second-largest market in the world by box office receipts. In 2014, the gross box office in China was
       <a href="/wiki/Renminbi" title="Renminbi">
        ¥
       </a>
       29.6 billion (
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">
        US$
       </a>
       4.82 billion), with domestic films having a share of 55%. The country is predicted to have the largest market in the world in 2017 or 2018.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frater_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Frater-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:2-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       China has also become a major hub of business for Hollywood studios.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2013, China's gross box office was ¥21.8 billion (US$3.6 billion), the second-largest film market in the world by box office receipts
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       whereas in 2014, China's box office gross was $4.8 Billion, being the second largest
       <a href="/wiki/Box_office" title="Box office">
        box office
       </a>
       grosser in film industry.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">
        United States
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: United States">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_States" title="Cinema of the United States">
        Cinema of the United States
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:228px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hollywood_Sign_(Zuschnitt).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6916" data-file-width="11065" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hollywood_Sign_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg/226px-Hollywood_Sign_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hollywood_Sign_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg/339px-Hollywood_Sign_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hollywood_Sign_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg/452px-Hollywood_Sign_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg 2x" width="226"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hollywood_Sign_(Zuschnitt).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Sign" title="Hollywood Sign">
          Hollywood Sign
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_States" title="Cinema of the United States">
        cinema of the United States
       </a>
       , often generally referred to as
       <b>
        Hollywood
       </b>
       , has had a profound effect on cinema across the world since the early 20th century. The United States cinema (Hollywood) is the oldest film industry in the world which originated more than 121 years ago and also the largest film industry in terms of revenue.
       <a href="/wiki/Hollywood" title="Hollywood">
        Hollywood
       </a>
       is the primary nexus of the U.S. film industry with established film study facilities such as the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Film_Institute" title="American Film Institute">
        American Film Institute
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LA_Film_School" title="LA Film School">
        LA Film School
       </a>
       and NYFA being established in the area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, four of the
       <a href="/wiki/Major_film_studio#Today's_Big_Six" title="Major film studio">
        six major film studios
       </a>
       are owned by
       <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">
        East Coast
       </a>
       companies. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Major_film_studios" title="Major film studios">
        major film studios
       </a>
       of Hollywood including
       <a href="/wiki/Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer" title="Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer">
        Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" title="20th Century Fox">
        20th Century Fox
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Pictures" title="Paramount Pictures">
        Paramount Pictures
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lightstorm_Entertainment" title="Lightstorm Entertainment">
        Lightstorm Entertainment
       </a>
       are the primary source of the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">
        most commercially successful movies in the world
       </a>
       , such as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Gone_with_the_Wind_(film)" title="Gone with the Wind (film)">
         Gone with the Wind
        </a>
       </i>
       (1939),
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">
         Star Wars
        </a>
       </i>
       (1977),
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">
         Titanic
        </a>
       </i>
       (1997), and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Avatar_(2009_film)" title="Avatar (2009 film)">
         Avatar
        </a>
       </i>
       (2009). Today, American film studios collectively generate several hundred movies every year, making the United States one of the most prolific producers of films in the world. Only
       <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">
        The Walt Disney Company
       </a>
       — which owns
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Studios_(division)" title="The Walt Disney Studios (division)">
        the Walt Disney Studios
       </a>
       — is fully based in
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">
        Southern California
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       And while
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Entertainment" title="Sony Pictures Entertainment">
        Sony Pictures Entertainment
       </a>
       is headquartered in Culver City, California, its parent company, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sony_Corporation" title="Sony Corporation">
        Sony Corporation
       </a>
       , is headquartered in
       <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">
        Tokyo
       </a>
       , Japan. Most shooting now takes place in
       <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
        California
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">
        New York
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">
        Louisiana
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">
        Georgia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">
        North Carolina
       </a>
       . Hollywood is the most popular film industry with the highest number of screens, and is the highest-grossing film industry in the world. Between 2009-2015, Hollywood consistently grossed $10 billion (or more) annually.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Hollywood's award ceremony, the
       <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">
        Academy Awards
       </a>
       , officially known as The Oscars, is held by the
       <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Motion_Picture_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences">
        Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences
       </a>
       (AMPAS) every year and a total of 2,947 Oscars have been awarded since the inception of the award.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The earliest documented account of an exhibition of projected motion pictures in the United States was in June 1894 in
       <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Indiana" title="Richmond, Indiana">
        Richmond, Indiana
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Francis_Jenkins" title="Charles Francis Jenkins">
        Charles Francis Jenkins
       </a>
       which makes
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_States" title="Cinema of the United States">
        United States cinema
       </a>
       the earliest cinema in the whole world. Jenkins used his Phantoscope to project his film before an audience of family, friends and reporters. The film featured a vaudeville dancer performing a Butterfly Dance. Jenkins and his new partner
       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Armat" title="Thomas Armat">
        Thomas Armat
       </a>
       modified the Phantoscope for exhibitions in temporary theaters at the Cotton States Exposition in the fall of 1895. The Phantoscope was later sold to
       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">
        Thomas Edison
       </a>
       , who changed the name of the projector to Edison's Vitascope.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:225px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nestor_studio_1911.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="765" data-file-width="962" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Nestor_studio_1911.jpg/223px-Nestor_studio_1911.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Nestor_studio_1911.jpg/335px-Nestor_studio_1911.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Nestor_studio_1911.jpg/446px-Nestor_studio_1911.jpg 2x" width="223"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nestor_studio_1911.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Nestor studio, 1911
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nestor_Studios" title="Nestor Studios">
        Nestor Studios
       </a>
       was Hollywood's first movie studio, founded on 27 October 1911 It was built by
       <a href="/wiki/David_Horsley" title="David Horsley">
        David Horsley
       </a>
       for Nestor Motion Picture Company. It was then owned and operated by
       <a href="/wiki/David_Horsley" title="David Horsley">
        David Horsley
       </a>
       and his brother, William Horsley. The first
       <a href="/wiki/Sound_stage" title="Sound stage">
        motion picture stage
       </a>
       in Hollywood was built behind the tavern. Other
       <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">
        East Coast
       </a>
       studios had moved production to Los Angeles, prior to Nestor's move west. The California weather allowed for year-round filming and the ambitious studio operated three principal divisions under its Canadian-born general manager,
       <a href="/wiki/Al_Christie" title="Al Christie">
        Al Christie
       </a>
       . Other
       <a href="/wiki/Filmmaking" title="Filmmaking">
        filmmakers
       </a>
       began opening studios in the
       <a href="/wiki/Hollywood" title="Hollywood">
        Hollywood
       </a>
       area. The Horsleys operated the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nestor_Studios" title="Nestor Studios">
        Nestor Studios
       </a>
       at the Sunset and Gower location until 20 May 1912, when the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universal_Studios" title="Universal Studios">
        Universal Studios
       </a>
       was formed, headed by
       <a href="/wiki/Carl_Laemmle" title="Carl Laemmle">
        Carl Laemmle
       </a>
       . Nestor, along with several other motion picture companies, including Laemmle's
       <a href="/wiki/Independent_Moving_Pictures" title="Independent Moving Pictures">
        Independent Moving Pictures
       </a>
       (IMP), was merged with Universal.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">
        United Kingdom
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Cinema of the United Kingdom">
        Cinema of the United Kingdom
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="India">
        India
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: India">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_India" title="Cinema of India">
        Cinema of India
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">
        Bollywood
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_West_Bengal" title="Cinema of West Bengal">
        Cinema of West Bengal
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_South_India" title="Cinema of South India">
        Cinema of South India
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Raja_Harishchandra.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="237" data-file-width="250" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Raja_Harishchandra.jpg/220px-Raja_Harishchandra.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4d/Raja_Harishchandra.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Raja_Harishchandra.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A scene from
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Raja_Harishchandra" title="Raja Harishchandra">
           Raja Harishchandra
          </a>
         </i>
         (1913) – credited as the first full-length Indian motion picture.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       India is the largest producer of films in the world and second oldest film industry in the world which originated around about 105 years ago.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Khanna2-140_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Khanna2-140-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2009 India produced a total of 2,961 films on celluloid; this figure includes 1,288 feature films.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBFC-ANR2009_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CBFC-ANR2009-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Besides being the largest producer of films in the world, India also has the largest number of admissions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Indian film industry is
       <a href="/wiki/Multilingualism" title="Multilingualism">
        multi-lingual
       </a>
       and the largest in the world in terms of ticket sales but 3rd largest in terms of revenue mainly due to having amongst the lowest ticket prices in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The industry is viewed mainly by a vast film-going Indian public, and Indian films have been gaining increasing popularity in the rest of the world—notably in countries with large numbers of expatriate Indians. Indian film industry is also the dominant source of movies and entertainment in its neighboring countries of
       <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">
        South Asia
       </a>
       . The largest film and most popular industry in India is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindi_cinema" title="Hindi cinema">
        Hindi film industry
       </a>
       mostly concentrated in
       <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">
        Mumbai
       </a>
       (Bombay),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and is commonly referred to as
       <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">
        Bollywood
       </a>
       , an amalgamation of Bombay an Hollywood. The other largest film industries are
       <a href="/wiki/Tamil_cinema" title="Tamil cinema">
        Tamil cinema
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Telugu_cinema" title="Telugu cinema">
        Telugu cinema
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kannada_cinema" title="Kannada cinema">
        Kannada cinema
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Malayalam_cinema" title="Malayalam cinema">
        Malayalam cinema
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bangla_cinema" title="Bangla cinema">
        Bangla cinema
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_West_Bengal" title="Cinema of West Bengal">
        cinema of West Bengal
       </a>
       ), which are located in
       <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">
        Chennai
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad" title="Hyderabad">
        Hyderabad
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">
        Bengaluru
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kochi" title="Kochi">
        Kochi
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">
        Kolkata
       </a>
       . The remaining majority portion is spread across northern, western, and southern India (with
       <a href="/wiki/Gujarati_cinema" title="Gujarati cinema">
        Gujarati
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Punjab" title="Cinema of Punjab">
        Punjabi
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marathi_Cinema" title="Marathi Cinema">
        Marathi
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oriya_cinema" title="Oriya cinema">
        Oriya
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri_cinema" title="Bhojpuri cinema">
        Bhojpuri
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assamese_Cinema" title="Assamese Cinema">
        Assamese Cinema
       </a>
       ). However, there are several smaller centers of Indian film industries in regional languages centered in the states where those languages are spoken. Indian films are made filled with musicals, action, romance, comedy, and an increasing number of special effects. It encloses a number of several artforms like Indian classical music, folk music of different regions throughout the country, Indian classical dance, folk dance and much more. It is even the place for number of artists from the Indian subcontinent to showcase their talent. The Indian film industry produces more than 1000 films a year. Bollywood is the largest portion of this and is viewed all over the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_Subcontinent" title="Indian Subcontinent">
        Indian Subcontinent
       </a>
       , and is increasingly popular in UK, United States, Australia, New Zealand,
       <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">
        Southeast Asia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">
        Africa
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gulf_countries" title="Gulf countries">
        Gulf countries
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        European countries
       </a>
       and China. The largest film studio complex in the world is
       <a href="/wiki/Ramoji_Film_City" title="Ramoji Film City">
        Ramoji Film City
       </a>
       located at
       <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad" title="Hyderabad">
        Hyderabad
       </a>
       , India, which opened in 1996 and measures 674 ha (1,666 acres). Comprising 47 sound stages, it has permanent sets ranging from railway stations to temples.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <br/>
      </p>
      <p>
       Bollywood represents 43% of Indian net box office revenue, while Telugu and Tamil cinema represent 36%, and the rest of the regional cinema constitute 21%, as of 2014.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_Indian_films" title="List of highest-grossing Indian films">
        highest grossing movie of India
       </a>
       is
       <a href="/wiki/Dangal_(film)" title="Dangal (film)">
        Dangal
       </a>
       which is also the 5th highest grossing non-English movie in the world.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Nigeria">
        Nigeria
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Nigeria">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Nigeria" title="Cinema of Nigeria">
        Cinema of Nigeria
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Nigeria" title="Cinema of Nigeria">
        cinema of Nigeria
       </a>
       , often referred to informally as
       <a href="/wiki/Nollywood" title="Nollywood">
        Nollywood
       </a>
       , is the second largest film industry, in terms of output, and the third largest, in terms of overall revenues generated.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-United_Nations_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-United_Nations-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Its history dates back to as early as the late 19th century and into the
       <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Nigeria" title="Colonial Nigeria">
        colonial era
       </a>
       in the early 20th century. The history and development of the Nigerian motion picture industry is sometimes generally classified in four main eras: the
       <a href="/wiki/Filmmaking_in_Colonial_Nigeria" title="Filmmaking in Colonial Nigeria">
        Colonial era
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Age_of_Nigerian_cinema" title="Golden Age of Nigerian cinema">
        Golden Age
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Video_film_era" title="Video film era">
        Video film era
       </a>
       and the emerging
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Nigerian_cinema" title="New Nigerian cinema">
        New Nigerian cinema
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Film as a medium first arrived Nigeria in the late 19th century, in the form of
       <a href="/wiki/Kinetoscope" title="Kinetoscope">
        peephole viewing of motion picture devices
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Modern_Ghana_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Modern_Ghana-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These were soon replaced in early 20th century with improved motion picture exhibition devices, with the first set of films screened at the Glover Memorial Hall in
       <a href="/wiki/Lagos" title="Lagos">
        Lagos
       </a>
       from 12 to 22 August 1903.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The earliest feature film made in Nigeria is the 1926
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Palaver_(1926_film)" title="Palaver (1926 film)">
         Palaver
        </a>
       </i>
       produced by
       <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Barkas" title="Geoffrey Barkas">
        Geoffrey Barkas
       </a>
       ; the film was also the first film ever to feature Nigerian actors in speaking roles.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ekenyerengozi,_Michael_Chima_31-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ekenyerengozi,_Michael_Chima-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Colonial_Film_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Colonial_Film-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first film entirely copyrighted to the Nigerian Film unit is
       <i>
        Fincho
       </i>
       (1957) by Sam Zebba; which is also the first Nigerian film to be
       <a href="/wiki/Color_motion_picture_film" title="Color motion picture film">
        shot in colour
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After Nigeria's independence in 1960, the cinema business rapidly expanded, with new cinema houses being established.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As a result, Nigerian content in theatres increased in the late 1960s into the 1970s, especially productions from Western Nigeria, owing to former
       <a href="/wiki/Theatre" title="Theatre">
        theatre
       </a>
       practitioners such as
       <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Ogunde" title="Hubert Ogunde">
        Hubert Ogunde
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Moses_Olaiya" title="Moses Olaiya">
        Moses Olaiya
       </a>
       transitioning into the big screen.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adegbola,_Tunde_2011_35-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Adegbola,_Tunde_2011-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1972, the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Yakubu_Gowon#Indigenization_Decree" title="Yakubu Gowon">
         Indigenization Decree
        </a>
       </i>
       was issued by
       <a href="/wiki/Yakubu_Gowon" title="Yakubu Gowon">
        Yakubu Gowon
       </a>
       , which demands the transfer of ownership of about a total of 300 film theatres from their foreign owners to Nigerians, which resulted in more Nigerians playing active roles in the cinema and film.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Obiaya,_Ikechukwu_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Obiaya,_Ikechukwu-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The oil boom of 1973 through 1978 also contributed immensely to the spontaneous boost of the cinema culture in Nigeria, as the increased purchasing power in Nigeria made a wide range of citizens to have disposable income to spend on cinema going and on home television sets.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After the decline of the Golden era, Nigerian film industry experienced a second major boom in the 1990s, supposedly marked by the release of the
       <a href="/wiki/Direct-to-video" title="Direct-to-video">
        direct-to-video
       </a>
       film
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Living_in_Bondage" title="Living in Bondage">
         Living in Bondage
        </a>
       </i>
       (1992); the industry peaked in the mid 2000s to become the second largest film industry in the world in terms of the number of annual film productions, placing it ahead of the
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_States" title="Cinema of the United States">
        United States
       </a>
       and behind only
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_cinema" title="Indian cinema">
        India
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-United_Nations_26-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-United_Nations-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The films started dominating screens across the African continent and by extension, the
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">
        Caribbeans
       </a>
       and the diaspora,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nollywood:_Lights,_camera,_Africa_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nollywood:_Lights,_camera,_Africa-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with the movies significantly influencing cultures, and the film actors becoming household names across the continent. The boom also led to a backlash against Nigerian films in several countries, bordering on theories such as the "Nigerialization of Africa".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since mid-2000s, the Nigerian cinema have undergone some restructuring to promote quality and professionalism, with
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Figurine" title="The Figurine">
         The Figurine
        </a>
       </i>
       (2009) widely regarded as marking the major turn around of contemporary Nigerian cinema. There has since been a resurgence in the proliferation of cinema establishments, and a steady
       <a href="/wiki/New_Nigerian_Cinema" title="New Nigerian Cinema">
        return of the cinema culture in Nigeria
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Economist_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-The_Economist-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The 2016 film
       <a href="/wiki/The_Wedding_Party_(2016_film)" title="The Wedding Party (2016 film)">
        The Wedding Party
       </a>
       , directed by
       <a href="/wiki/Kemi_Adetiba" title="Kemi Adetiba">
        Kemi Adetiba
       </a>
       , is the highest grossing Nollywood film of all time.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Egypt">
        Egypt
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Egypt">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Egypt" title="Cinema of Egypt">
        Cinema of Egypt
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Egyptian cinema is the flourishing cinema of North Africa. Since 1976, Cairo has held the annual
       <a href="/wiki/Cairo_International_Film_Festival" title="Cairo International Film Festival">
        Cairo International Film Festival
       </a>
       (CIFF), which is accredited by the International Federation of Film Producers Association. Most of today’s Egyptian movies and TV series are produced in the Egyptian Media Production City which is equipped with the latest equipment for shooting in outdoor and indoor studios.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It includes about 64 high tech studios. Censorship, formerly an obstacle to freedom of expression, has decreased remarkably. The Egyptian cinema has witnessed a remarkable shift in terms of the taboos it may address. It has begun to tackle boldly issues ranging from sexual issues
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       to heavy government criticism.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The 1940s, 1950s and the 1960s are generally considered the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_age" title="Golden age">
        golden age
       </a>
       of Egyptian cinema. As in the West, films responded to the popular imagination, with most falling into predictable
       <a href="/wiki/Film_genre" title="Film genre">
        genres
       </a>
       (happy endings being the norm), and many actors making careers out of playing strongly typed parts. In the words of one critic, "If an Egyptian film intended for popular audiences lacked any of these prerequisites, it constituted a betrayal of the unwritten contract with the spectator, the results of which would manifest themselves in the box office."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-retrospection_45-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-retrospection-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since the 1990s, Egypt's cinema has gone in separate directions. Smaller
       <a href="/wiki/Art_film" title="Art film">
        art films
       </a>
       attract some international attention but sparse attendance at home. Popular films, often broad comedies such as
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/What_A_Lie!_(film)" title="What A Lie! (film)">
         What A Lie!
        </a>
       </i>
       , and the extremely profitable works of comedian
       <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Saad" title="Mohamed Saad">
        Mohamed Saad
       </a>
       , battle to hold audiences either drawn to Western films or, increasingly, wary of the perceived immorality of film.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-story_46-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-story-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Iran">
        Iran
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Iran">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Iran" title="Cinema of Iran">
        Cinema of Iran
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        cinema of Iran
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">
        Persian
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        سینمای ایران
       </i>
       ) or
       <b>
        cinema of Persia
       </b>
       refers to the cinema and film industries in
       <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">
        Iran
       </a>
       which produce a variety of commercial films annually. Iranian
       <a href="/wiki/Art_film" title="Art film">
        art films
       </a>
       have garnered international fame and now enjoy a global following.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-internews1_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-internews1-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Along with China, Iran has been lauded as one of the best exporters of cinema in the 1990s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some critics now rank Iran as the world's most important national cinema, artistically, with a significance that invites comparison to
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_neorealism" title="Italian neorealism">
        Italian neorealism
       </a>
       and similar movements in past decades.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-internews1_47-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-internews1-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A range of international film festivals have honored Iranian cinema in the last twenty years. World-renowned Austrian filmmaker
       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Haneke" title="Michael Haneke">
        Michael Haneke
       </a>
       and German filmmaker
       <a href="/wiki/Werner_Herzog" title="Werner Herzog">
        Werner Herzog
       </a>
       , along with many film critics from around the world, have praised Iranian cinema as one of the world's most important artistic cinemas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">
        Japan
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Japan">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       See
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Japan" title="Cinema of Japan">
        Cinema of Japan
       </a>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Korea">
        Korea
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Korea">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Korea" title="Cinema of Korea">
        Cinema of Korea
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_South_Korea" title="Cinema of South Korea">
        Cinema of South Korea
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_North_Korea" title="Cinema of North Korea">
        Cinema of North Korea
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The term "
       <b>
        cinema of Korea
       </b>
       " (or "
       <b>
        Korean cinema
       </b>
       ") encompasses the motion picture industries of
       <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">
        North
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">
        South Korea
       </a>
       . As with all aspects of Korean life during the past century, the film industry has often been at the mercy of political events, from the late
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joseon_dynasty" title="Joseon dynasty">
        Joseon dynasty
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">
        the Korean War
       </a>
       to domestic governmental interference. While both countries have relatively robust film industries today, only South Korean films have achieved wide international acclaim. North Korean films tend to portray their communist or revolutionary themes.
      </p>
      <p>
       South Korean films enjoyed a "Golden age" during the late 1950s, and 1960s, but by the 1970s had become generally considered to be of low quality. Nonetheless, by 2005 South Korea had become one of few nations to watch more domestic than imported films in theatres
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       due largely to laws placing limits on the number of foreign films able to be shown per theatre per year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jameson_51-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Jameson-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the theaters, Korean films must be played for 73 days per year since 2006. On cable TV 25% domestic film quota will be reduced to 20% after KOR-US FTA.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <b>
        cinema of South Korea
       </b>
       had a total box office gross in the country in 2015 of
       <a href="/wiki/South_Korean_won" title="South Korean won">
        ₩
       </a>
       884 billion and had 113,000,000 admissions, 52% of the total admissions.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hong_Kong">
        Hong Kong
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Hong Kong">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LaiMan-Wai.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="445" data-file-width="460" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/LaiMan-Wai.jpg/200px-LaiMan-Wai.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/LaiMan-Wai.jpg/300px-LaiMan-Wai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/LaiMan-Wai.jpg/400px-LaiMan-Wai.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LaiMan-Wai.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Zhuangzi_Tests_His_Wife" title="Zhuangzi Tests His Wife">
           Zhuangzi Tests His Wife
          </a>
         </i>
         (1913) is credited as the first Hong Kong feature film
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Hong_Kong" title="Cinema of Hong Kong">
        Cinema of Hong Kong
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_China" title="Cinema of China">
        Cinema of China
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/East_Asian_cinema" title="East Asian cinema">
        East Asian cinema
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">
        Hong Kong
       </a>
       is a filmmaking hub for the Chinese-speaking world (including the worldwide
       <a href="/wiki/Diaspora" title="Diaspora">
        diaspora
       </a>
       ) and East Asia in general. For decades it was the third largest motion picture industry in the world (after Bollywood and Hollywood) and the second largest exporter of films.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Despite an industry crisis starting in the mid-1990s and Hong Kong's return to Chinese sovereignty in July 1997 Hong Kong film has retained much of its distinctive identity and continues to play a prominent part on the world cinema stage. Unlike many film industries, Hong Kong has enjoyed little to no direct government support, through either subsidies or import quotas. It has always been a thoroughly commercial cinema, concentrating on crowd-pleasing
       <a href="/wiki/Film_genre" title="Film genre">
        genres
       </a>
       , like comedy and action, and heavily reliant on formulas, sequels and remakes. Typically of commercial cinemas, its heart is a highly developed
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Star_system_(film)" title="Star system (film)">
        star system
       </a>
       , which in this case also features substantial overlap with the
       <a href="/wiki/Cantopop" title="Cantopop">
        pop music industry
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">
        Turkey
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Turkey">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Yeşilçam film industry is firmly established as the second largest
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        European
       </a>
       theatrical growth market and the 7th largest
       <a href="/wiki/Theatre" title="Theatre">
        theatrical
       </a>
       market in terms of admissions, only superseded by the ‘big 5’ EU markets and the Russian Federation. The Turkish film market also stands out in the pan-European landscape as the only market where
       <a href="/wiki/Nation" title="Nation">
        national
       </a>
       films regularly outperform
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        US
       </a>
       films.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It had 1.2 million number of admissions in film industry and 87
       <a href="/wiki/Feature_film" title="Feature film">
        feature films
       </a>
       were released in the year 2013.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Because of the exceptional
       <a href="/wiki/Box_office" title="Box office">
        box office
       </a>
       success of Turkish films on the domestic market, the estimated 12.9 million admissions generated on non-national
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        European
       </a>
       markets only account for 7% of total admissions to Turkish films in Europe (including Turkey) between 2004 and 2013. This is the third lowest share among the 30 European markets for which such data are available and clearly illustrates the strong dependence of
       <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">
        Turkish
       </a>
       films on the domestic market, a feature which is shared by
       <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">
        Polish
       </a>
       and Russian films.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Over the past ten years an increasing number of Turkish films and filmmakers have been selected for
       <a href="/wiki/International" title="International">
        international
       </a>
       film festivals and received a large number of awards, like
       <a href="/wiki/Winter_Sleep_(film)" title="Winter Sleep (film)">
        Kış Uykusu
       </a>
       (Winter's Sleep) won
       <a href="/wiki/Cannes_Film_Festival" title="Cannes Film Festival">
        Cannes Film Festival
       </a>
       Award for Best Film in 2014.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In terms of box office Turkey still ranks behind the
       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">
        Netherlands
       </a>
       with just over EUR 200 million as Europe's eight largest box office market ahead of
       <a href="/wiki/Sweden_men%27s_national_ice_hockey_team" title="Sweden men's national ice hockey team">
        Sweden
       </a>
       and Switzerland with a clear gap to the top 6 markets all of which registered GBO between EUR 504 million (Spain) up to over EUR 1 billion in France, the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
        UK
       </a>
       , Germany and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" title="Russian Federation">
        Russian Federation
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cinema going is comparatively cheap in Turkey. In 2013 a
       <a href="/wiki/Movie_theater" title="Movie theater">
        cinema
       </a>
       ticket cost on average EUR 4.0 in Turkey, and this is estimated to be the lowest average ticket price - measured in Euro - in
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        Europe
       </a>
       , marginally cheaper than in several Central and
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">
        Eastern European
       </a>
       markets like Croatia, Romania, Lithuania or Bulgaria.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KANZLER_2014_72_59-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-KANZLER_2014_72-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       When comparing ticket prices in Euro, one of course has to take into consideration that these comparisons are significantly affected by fluctuations in the exchange rates of the various
       <a href="/wiki/Currency" title="Currency">
        currencies
       </a>
       . Because of devaluation of the
       <a href="/wiki/Turkish_lira" title="Turkish lira">
        Turkish Lira
       </a>
       against the Euro, average ticket prices measured in
       <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">
        Euro
       </a>
       remained fairly stable over the past 10 years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KANZLER_2014_72_59-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-KANZLER_2014_72-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">
        Pakistan
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Pakistan">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Pakistan" title="Cinema of Pakistan">
        Cinema of Pakistan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lollywood" title="Lollywood">
        Lollywood
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        cinema of Pakistan
       </b>
       , or simply,
       <b>
        Pakistani cinema
       </b>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urdu_language" title="Urdu language">
        Urdu
       </a>
       :
       <span dir="rtl" lang="ur" xml:lang="ur">
        <span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" style="font-family: 'Jameel Noori Nastaleeq', 'Urdu Typesetting', 'Noto Nastaliq Urdu', 'Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft', 'Hussaini Nastaleeq', 'AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq', IranNastaliq, 'Awami Nastaliq', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta3', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta2', 'Awami Nastaliq Beta1', 'Nafees Nastaleeq', 'Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01', 'Pak Nastaleeq', 'PDMS_Jauhar', 'Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq'; font-size: 125%; font-style: normal;" title="Nastaliq">
         پاکستانی سنیما
        </span>
        ‬
       </span>
       ‎) refers to
       <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">
        Pakistan
       </a>
       's film industry. Most of the feature films shot in Pakistan are in
       <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">
        Urdu
       </a>
       , the national language, but may also include films in English, the official language, and regional languages such as
       <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_language" title="Punjabi language">
        Punjabi
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pashto_language" title="Pashto language">
        Pashto
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Balochi_language" title="Balochi language">
        Balochi
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Sindhi_language" title="Sindhi language">
        Sindhi
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Lahore" title="Lahore">
        Lahore
       </a>
       was the epicentre of Pakistani cinema and Pakistan's largest film industry was
       <a href="/wiki/Lollywood" title="Lollywood">
        Lollywood
       </a>
       after The film industry again shifted its base in
       <a href="/wiki/Karachi" title="Karachi">
        Karachi
       </a>
       &amp; by 2007
       <a href="/wiki/Karachi" title="Karachi">
        Karachi
       </a>
       has permanently become the Pakistani film and showbiz industry's headquarters.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Before the separation of Bangladesh, Pakistan had three main film production centres:
       <a href="/wiki/Lahore" title="Lahore">
        Lahore
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Karachi" title="Karachi">
        Karachi
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Dhaka" title="Dhaka">
        Dhaka
       </a>
       . The regime of
       <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Zia-ul-Haq" title="Muhammad Zia-ul-Haq">
        Muhammad Zia-ul-Haq
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Video_cassette_recorder" title="Video cassette recorder">
        VCRs
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Film_piracy" title="Film piracy">
        film piracy
       </a>
       , the introduction of entertainment taxes, strict laws based upon ultra-conservative jurisprudence, was an obstacle to the industry's growth.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dawn.com_60-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-dawn.com-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Once thriving, the cinema in Pakistan had a sudden collapse in the 1980s and by the 2000s "an industry that once produced an average of 80 films annually was now struggling to even churn out more than two films a year.".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, the industry has recently made a dramatic and remarkable comeback, evident from the fact that 18 of the 21 highest grossing Pakistani movies were released from 2013 through to the present, with Pakistani films frequently outcompeting Bollywood movies for the Pakistani audience, the industry is supported by Pakistani channels such as ARY and Geo whose entertainment divisions have invested significantly in Pakistani cinema when expanding from providing news and entertainment on TV channels, the lifting of strict regulations on production of films and reduction of taxes on cinemas helped to fuel an expansion across the industry from which the film industry has seen a revival.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Bangladesh">
        Bangladesh
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Bangladesh">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Bangladesh" title="Cinema of Bangladesh">
        Cinema of Bangladesh
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dhallywood" title="Dhallywood">
        Dhallywood
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        cinema of Bangladesh
       </b>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">
        Bengali
       </a>
       language film industry based in
       <a href="/wiki/Dhaka" title="Dhaka">
        Dhaka
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">
        Bangladesh
       </a>
       . The industry often has been a significant film industry since the early 1970s. The word "Dhallywood" is a portmanteau of the words Dhaka and
       <a href="/wiki/Hollywood" title="Hollywood">
        Hollywood
       </a>
       . The dominant style of Bangladeshi cinema is
       <a href="/wiki/Melodrama" title="Melodrama">
        Melodramatic cinema
       </a>
       , which developed from 1947 to 1990 and characterizes most films to this day. Cinema was introduced in Bangladesh in 1898 by Bradford Bioscope Company, credited to have arranged the first film release in Bangladesh. Between 1913 and 1914, the first production company named Picture House was opened. A short silent film titled
       <i>
        Sukumari
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        The Good Girl
       </i>
       ) was the first produced film in the region during 1928. The first full-length film
       <i>
        The Last Kiss
       </i>
       , was released in 1931. From the separation of Bangladesh from Pakistan, Dhaka is the center of Bangladeshi film industry, and generated the majority share of revenue, production and audiences. The 1960s, 1970s, 1980s and the first half of the 1990s were the golden years for Bangladeshi films as the industry produced many successful films.
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Mukh_O_Mukhosh" title="Mukh O Mukhosh">
         The Face and the Mask
        </a>
       </i>
       , the first Bengali language Bangladeshi full-length feature film was produced in 1956.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cholochitro_63-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cholochitro-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mukh_O_Mukhosh_64-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mukh_O_Mukhosh-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Directors such as
       <a href="/wiki/Fateh_Lohani" title="Fateh Lohani">
        Fateh Lohani
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Zahir_Raihan" title="Zahir Raihan">
        Zahir Raihan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alamgir_Kabir_(film_maker)" title="Alamgir Kabir (film maker)">
        Alamgir Kabir
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Khan_Ataur_Rahman" title="Khan Ataur Rahman">
        Khan Ataur Rahman
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Subhash_Dutta" title="Subhash Dutta">
        Subhash Dutta
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ritwik_Ghatak" title="Ritwik Ghatak">
        Ritwik Ghatak
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ehtesham" title="Ehtesham">
        Ehtesham
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chashi_Nazrul_Islam" title="Chashi Nazrul Islam">
        Chashi Nazrul Islam
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_al_Mamun" title="Abdullah al Mamun">
        Abdullah al Mamun
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Niamat_Ali" title="Sheikh Niamat Ali">
        Sheikh Niamat Ali
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gazi_Mazharul_Anwar" title="Gazi Mazharul Anwar">
        Gazi Mazharul Anwar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tanvir_Mokammel" title="Tanvir Mokammel">
        Tanvir Mokammel
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tareque_Masud" title="Tareque Masud">
        Tareque Masud
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Morshedul_Islam" title="Morshedul Islam">
        Morshedul Islam
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Humayun_Ahmed" title="Humayun Ahmed">
        Humayun Ahmed
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gias_Uddin_Selim" title="Gias Uddin Selim">
        Gias Uddin Selim
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mostofa_Sarwar_Farooki" title="Mostofa Sarwar Farooki">
        Mostofa Sarwar Farooki
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Zahidur_Rahman_Anjan" title="Zahidur Rahman Anjan">
        Zahidur Rahman Anjan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kamar_Ahmed_Saimon" title="Kamar Ahmed Saimon">
        Kamar Ahmed Saimon
       </a>
       , Bijon Imtiaz,
       <a href="/wiki/Amitabh_Reza_Chowdhury" title="Amitabh Reza Chowdhury">
        Amitabh Reza Chowdhury
       </a>
       and others have made significant contributions to Bangladeshi
       <a href="/wiki/Mainstream" title="Mainstream">
        mainstream
       </a>
       cinema,
       <a href="/wiki/Parallel_cinema" title="Parallel cinema">
        parallel cinema
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Art_film" title="Art film">
        art films
       </a>
       and won global acclaim.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Indonesia">
        Indonesia
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Indonesia">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Indonesia" title="Cinema of Indonesia">
        Cinema of Indonesia
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The biggest film studios in
       <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">
        Southeast Asia
       </a>
       has been soft opened on 5 November 2011 on 10 hectares of land in
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nongsa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nongsa (page does not exist)">
        Nongsa
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Batam_Island" title="Batam Island">
        Batam Island
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">
        Indonesia
       </a>
       . Infinite Frameworks (IFW) is a
       <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">
        Singapore
       </a>
       -based company (closed to Batam Island) which easy to approach or be approached by international clients and is owned by a consortium with 90 percent of it hold by Indonesian businessman and movie producer, Mike Wiluan.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2010-2011, due to the substantial increase in value added tax applied to foreign films, cinemas no longer have access to many foreign films, including Oscar-winning films. Foreign films include major box offices from the west, and other major film producers of the world. This has caused a massive ripple effect on the country's economy. It is assumed that this increases the purchase of unlicensed DVDs. However, even copyright violating DVDs now take longer to obtain. The minimum cost to view a foreign film not screened locally, is 1 million Rupiah. This is equivalent to US$100, as it includes a plane ticket to Singapore.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
