        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Locally made film quality has gone up in 2012, this is attested by the international release of films such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Raid:_Redemption" title="The Raid: Redemption">
        The Raid: Redemption
       </a>
       , Modus Anomali, Dilema, Lovely Man,
       <a href="/wiki/Java_Heat" title="Java Heat">
        Java Heat
       </a>
       , etc.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Trinidad_and_Tobago">
        Trinidad and Tobago
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Trinidad and Tobago">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago_films" title="List of Trinidad and Tobago films">
        List of Trinidad and Tobago films
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Trinidad and Tobago’s film sector began emerging in the late fifties to early sixties and by the late seventies, there were a handful of local productions, both feature film and television.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ttfilmcompany_67-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ttfilmcompany-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first full-length feature film to be produced in
       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">
        Trinidad and Tobago
       </a>
       was “The Right and the Wrong” (1970) by Indian director/writer/producer, Harbance Kumar. The screenplay was written by the Trinidadian playwright, Freddie Kissoon.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fredkissoon_68-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-fredkissoon-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The rest of the 20th century saw a couple more feature films being made in the country, with “
       <a href="/wiki/Bim" title="Bim">
        Bim
       </a>
       ” (1974), being singled out by Bruce Paddington as "one of the most important films to be produced in Trinidad and Tobago….and one of the classics of Caribbean cinema.”
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbeat_69-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cbeat-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was one of the first films to feature an almost entirely Trinidadian cast and crew.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bimfans_70-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-bimfans-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There was a rise in Trinidadian film production in the 2000s. Movies such as “Ivan the Terrible” (2004), “
       <a href="/wiki/SistaGod" title="SistaGod">
        SistaGod
       </a>
       ” (2006), “I’m Santana: The Movie” (2012) and “God Loves the Fighter” (2013) were released both locally and internationally. “SistaGod” had its world premiere at the
       <a href="/wiki/2006_Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="2006 Toronto International Film Festival">
        2006 Toronto International Film Festival
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Film_Company" title="Trinidad and Tobago Film Company">
        Trinidad and Tobago Film Company
       </a>
       is the national agency that was established in 2006 to further development of the film industry. Trinidad and Tobago puts on a number of film festivals which are organized by different committees and organizations. These include the Secondary Schools Short Film Festival and Smartphone Film Festival organized by Trinidad and Tobago Film Company. There is also an annual
       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_Film_Festival" title="Trinidad and Tobago Film Festival">
        Trinidad and Tobago Film Festival
       </a>
       which runs for two weeks in the latter half of September.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Nepal">
        Nepal
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Nepal">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kallywood" title="Kallywood">
        Kallywood
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Nepali film does not have a very long movie history, but the industry has its own place in the cultural heritage of the country. It is often referred to as 'Nepali Chalchitra' (which translates to "Nepali movies" in English). The terms Kollywood and Kallywood are also used, as a portmanteau of "Kathmandu" and "Hollywood"; "Kollywood" however is more frequently used to refer to Tamil cinema.[1]
       <a href="/wiki/Chhakka_Panja" title="Chhakka Panja">
        Chhakka Panja
       </a>
       has been considered the highest-grossing movie of all time in Nepali Movie Industry and Kohinoor the second highest. Nepali movies has recently begun receiving international acclaim with films such as
       <a href="/wiki/The_Black_Hen" title="The Black Hen">
        The Black Hen
       </a>
       (2015),
       <a href="/wiki/Kagbeni_(film)" title="Kagbeni (film)">
        Kagbeni
       </a>
       (2006) and others. Nepali feature film
       <a href="/wiki/White_Sun" title="White Sun">
        White Sun
       </a>
       (Seto Surya) has bagged the Best Film award at
       <a class="external text" href="http://sgiff.com/" rel="nofollow">
        the 27th Singapore International Film Festival
       </a>
       (SGIFF)(2016).
      </p>
      <p>
       The Film Development Board (FDB) was established by the Government of Nepal for the development and promotion of the Nepali film industry. The Board is a liaison to facilitate the conceptualization, making, distribution and exhibition of Nepali films nationally. The Board attempts to bridge the gap between film entrepreneurship and government bureaucracy. The Board is a balance between the people at large, the government, and the process of film making. It is intended to act as the safeguard of the interests of the people, the watchdog of the government, and the advocate of filmmakers.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_film" title="History of film">
        History of film
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Story-of-the-kelly-gang-capture-1906.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="352" data-file-width="498" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Story-of-the-kelly-gang-capture-1906.jpg/220px-Story-of-the-kelly-gang-capture-1906.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Story-of-the-kelly-gang-capture-1906.jpg/330px-Story-of-the-kelly-gang-capture-1906.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Story-of-the-kelly-gang-capture-1906.jpg/440px-Story-of-the-kelly-gang-capture-1906.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Story-of-the-kelly-gang-capture-1906.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Still_frame" title="Still frame">
          still
         </a>
         from
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/The_Story_of_the_Kelly_Gang" title="The Story of the Kelly Gang">
           The Story of the Kelly Gang
          </a>
         </i>
         (Australia, 1906; 80 min.)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The first
       <a href="/wiki/Feature_film" title="Feature film">
        feature film
       </a>
       to be made was the 1906 Australian silent
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Story_of_the_Kelly_Gang" title="The Story of the Kelly Gang">
         The Story of the Kelly Gang
        </a>
       </i>
       , an account of the notorious gang led by
       <a href="/wiki/Ned_Kelly" title="Ned Kelly">
        Ned Kelly
       </a>
       that was directed and produced by the
       <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">
        Melburnians
       </a>
       Dan Barry and
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Tait_(film_director)" title="Charles Tait (film director)">
        Charles Tait
       </a>
       . It ran, continuously, for eighty minutes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By the time other countries began making feature films, in 1911, a further fifteen feature-length films had been made in Australia.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2007)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the early 1910s, the film industry had fully emerged with D.W. Griffith's
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Birth_of_a_Nation" title="The Birth of a Nation">
         The Birth of a Nation
        </a>
       </i>
       . Also in the early 1900s motion picture production companies from New York and New Jersey started moving to California because of the good weather and longer days. Although electric lights existed at that time, none were powerful enough to adequately expose film; the best source of illumination for movie production was natural sunlight. Besides the moderate, dry climate, they were also drawn to the state because of its open spaces and wide variety of natural scenery.
      </p>
      <p>
       Another reason was the distance of Southern California from New Jersey, making it more difficult for
       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">
        Thomas Edison
       </a>
       to enforce his motion picture patents. At the time, Edison owned almost all the patents relevant to motion picture production and, in the East, movie producers acting independently of Edison's Motion Picture Patents Company were often sued or enjoined by Edison and his agents. Thus, movie makers working on the West Coast could work independently of Edison's control. If he sent agents to California, word would usually reach Los Angeles before the agents did and the movie makers could escape to nearby Mexico.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2007)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hollywood">
        Hollywood
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Hollywood">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Hollywood is the oldest film industry in the world which was originated 121 years ago. The earliest documented account of an exhibition of projected motion pictures in the United States was in June 1894 in
       <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_Indiana" title="Richmond, Indiana">
        Richmond, Indiana
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Francis_Jenkins" title="Charles Francis Jenkins">
        Charles Francis Jenkins
       </a>
       . The first
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Movie_studio" title="Movie studio">
        movie studio
       </a>
       in the Hollywood area,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nestor_Studios" title="Nestor Studios">
        Nestor Studios
       </a>
       , was founded in 1911 by
       <a href="/wiki/Al_Christie" title="Al Christie">
        Al Christie
       </a>
       for
       <a href="/wiki/David_Horsley" title="David Horsley">
        David Horsley
       </a>
       in an old building on the northwest corner of
       <a href="/wiki/Sunset_Boulevard" title="Sunset Boulevard">
        Sunset Boulevard
       </a>
       and Gower Street. In the same year, another fifteen Independents settled in Hollywood. Hollywood came to be so strongly associated with the film industry that the word "Hollywood" came to be used colloquially to refer to the entire industry.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1913
       <a href="/wiki/Cecil_B._DeMille" title="Cecil B. DeMille">
        Cecil B. DeMille
       </a>
       , in association with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesse_Lasky" title="Jesse Lasky">
        Jesse Lasky
       </a>
       , leased a barn with studio facilities on the southeast corner of Selma and Vine Streets from the Burns and Revier Studio and Laboratory, which had been established there. DeMille then began production of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Squaw_Man_(1914_film)" title="The Squaw Man (1914 film)">
         The Squaw Man
        </a>
       </i>
       (1914). It became known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Lasky-DeMille_Barn" title="Lasky-DeMille Barn">
        Lasky-DeMille Barn
       </a>
       and is currently the location of the
       <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Heritage_Museum" title="Hollywood Heritage Museum">
        Hollywood Heritage Museum
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Chaplin" title="Charlie Chaplin">
        Charlie Chaplin
       </a>
       Studios, on the northeast corner of La Brea and De Longpre Avenues just south of Sunset Boulevard, was built in 1917. It has had many owners after 1953, including Kling Studios, which housed production for the
       <a href="/wiki/Adventures_of_Superman_(TV_series)" title="Adventures of Superman (TV series)">
        <i>
         Superman
        </i>
        TV series
       </a>
       with
       <a href="/wiki/George_Reeves" title="George Reeves">
        George Reeves
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Skelton" title="Red Skelton">
        Red Skelton
       </a>
       , who used the
       <a href="/wiki/Sound_stage" title="Sound stage">
        sound stages
       </a>
       for his
       <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">
        CBS
       </a>
       TV
       <a href="/wiki/Variety_show" title="Variety show">
        variety show
       </a>
       ; and CBS, who filmed the TV series
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Perry_Mason_(TV_series)" title="Perry Mason (TV series)">
         Perry Mason
        </a>
       </i>
       with
       <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Burr" title="Raymond Burr">
        Raymond Burr
       </a>
       there. It has also been owned by
       <a href="/wiki/Herb_Alpert" title="Herb Alpert">
        Herb Alpert
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/A%26M_Records" title="A&amp;M Records">
        A&amp;M Records
       </a>
       and Tijuana Brass Enterprises. It is currently The
       <a href="/wiki/Jim_Henson" title="Jim Henson">
        Jim Henson
       </a>
       Company, home of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muppets" title="Muppets">
        Muppets
       </a>
       . In 1969 The Los Angeles Cultural Heritage Board named the studio a historical cultural monument.
      </p>
      <p>
       The famous
       <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Sign" title="Hollywood Sign">
        Hollywood Sign
       </a>
       originally read "Hollywoodland." It was erected in 1923 to advertise a new housing development in the hills above Hollywood. For several years the sign was left to deteriorate. In 1949 the Hollywood Chamber of Commerce stepped in and offered to remove the last four letters and repair the rest.
      </p>
      <p>
       The sign, located at the top of Mount Lee, is now a registered trademark and cannot be used without the permission of the Hollywood Chamber of Commerce, which also manages the venerable
       <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">
        Walk of Fame
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The first
       <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">
        Academy Awards
       </a>
       presentation ceremony took place on 16 May 1929, during a banquet held in the Blossom Room of the Hollywood Roosevelt Hotel on Hollywood Boulevard. Tickets were
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">
        USD
       </a>
       $10.00
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       and there were 250 people in attendance.
      </p>
      <p>
       From about 1930 five major Hollywood movie studios from all over the Los Angeles area,
       <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Pictures" title="Paramount Pictures">
        Paramount
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RKO" title="RKO">
        RKO
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" title="20th Century Fox">
        20th Century Fox
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer" title="Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer">
        Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">
        Warner Bros.
       </a>
       , owned large, grand
       <a href="/wiki/Movie_theater" title="Movie theater">
        theaters
       </a>
       throughout the country for the exhibition of their movies. The period between the years 1927 (the effective end of the silent era) to 1948 is considered the age of the "Hollywood studio system", or, in a more common term, the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_cinema#The_Golden_Age_of_Hollywood" title="History of cinema">
         Golden Age of Hollywood
        </a>
       </i>
       . In a
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_v._Paramount_Pictures,_Inc." title="United States v. Paramount Pictures, Inc.">
        landmark 1948 court decision
       </a>
       , the Supreme Court ruled that movie studios could not own theaters and play only the movies of their studio and
       <a href="/wiki/Movie_star" title="Movie star">
        movie stars
       </a>
       , thus an era of Hollywood history had unofficially ended. By the mid-1950s, when television proved a profitable enterprise that was here to stay, movie studios started also being used for the production of programming in that medium, which is still the norm today.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Bollywood">
        Bollywood
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Bollywood">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">
        Bollywood
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_scene_from_film,_Raja_Harishchandra,_1913.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="382" data-file-width="512" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/A_scene_from_film%2C_Raja_Harishchandra%2C_1913.jpg/220px-A_scene_from_film%2C_Raja_Harishchandra%2C_1913.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/A_scene_from_film%2C_Raja_Harishchandra%2C_1913.jpg/330px-A_scene_from_film%2C_Raja_Harishchandra%2C_1913.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/A_scene_from_film%2C_Raja_Harishchandra%2C_1913.jpg/440px-A_scene_from_film%2C_Raja_Harishchandra%2C_1913.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_scene_from_film,_Raja_Harishchandra,_1913.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A shot from
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Raja_Harishchandra" title="Raja Harishchandra">
           Raja Harishchandra
          </a>
         </i>
         (1913), the first film of
         <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">
          Bollywood
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">
        Bollywood
       </a>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">
        Hindi
       </a>
       -language film industry based in
       <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">
        Mumbai
       </a>
       (formerly known as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bombay" title="Bombay">
        Bombay
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra" title="Maharashtra">
        Maharashtra
       </a>
       , India. The term is often incorrectly used to refer to the whole of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_cinema" title="Indian cinema">
        Indian cinema
       </a>
       ; however, it is only a part of the total
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_film" title="Indian film">
        Indian film
       </a>
       industry, which includes other production centres producing films in multiple languages.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Bollywood is the largest film producer in India and one of the largest centres of film production in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Bollywood is formally referred to as Hindi cinema.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica_77-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-britannica-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Linguistically, Bollywood films tend to use a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colloquial" title="Colloquial">
        colloquial
       </a>
       dialect of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindi-Urdu" title="Hindi-Urdu">
        Hindi-Urdu
       </a>
       , or
       <a href="/wiki/Hindustani_language" title="Hindustani language">
        Hindustani
       </a>
       , mutually intelligible to both Hindi and
       <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">
        Urdu
       </a>
       speakers,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scienceandmediamuseum_78-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-scienceandmediamuseum-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Akhtar_79-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Akhtar-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-film-world_80-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-film-world-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       while modern Bollywood films also increasingly incorporate elements of
       <a href="/wiki/Hinglish" title="Hinglish">
        Hinglish
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scienceandmediamuseum_78-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-scienceandmediamuseum-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <i>
        The Wrestlers
       </i>
       (1899) and
       <i>
        The Man and His Monkeys
       </i>
       (1899), directed and produced by Harischandra Sakharam Bhatawdekar (
       <a href="/wiki/H._S._Bhatavdekar" title="H. S. Bhatavdekar">
        H. S. Bhatavdekar
       </a>
       ), were the first two films made by Indian filmmakers, which were both short films. He was also the first Indian filmmaker to direct and produce the first documentary and news related film, titled
       <i>
        The Landing of Sir M.M. Bhownuggree
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <i>
        Pundalik
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Shree_Pundalik" title="Shree Pundalik">
         Shree Pundalik
        </a>
       </i>
       ) (1912), by
       <a href="/wiki/Dadasaheb_Torne" title="Dadasaheb Torne">
        Dadasaheb Torne
       </a>
       alias Rama Chandra Gopal, and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Raja_Harishchandra" title="Raja Harishchandra">
         Raja Harishchandra
        </a>
       </i>
       (1913), by
       <a href="/wiki/Dadasaheb_Phalke" title="Dadasaheb Phalke">
        Dadasaheb Phalke
       </a>
       , were the first and second silent feature films respectively made in India.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guinness_Books_81-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Guinness_Books-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dainik_Asam_Assamese_daily_82-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Dainik_Asam_Assamese_daily-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Firoze_Rangoonwalla_84-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Firoze_Rangoonwalla-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By the 1930s the industry was producing more than 200 films per annum.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica2_85-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-britannica2-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first Indian sound film,
       <a href="/wiki/Ardeshir_Irani" title="Ardeshir Irani">
        Ardeshir Irani
       </a>
       's
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Alam_Ara" title="Alam Ara">
         Alam Ara
        </a>
       </i>
       (1931), was a major commercial success.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There was clearly a huge market for talkies and musicals; Bollywood and all the regional film industries quickly switched to sound filming.
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Joymoti_(1935_film)" title="Joymoti (1935 film)">
         Joymoti (1935 film)
        </a>
       </i>
       by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jyoti_Prasad_Agarwalla" title="Jyoti Prasad Agarwalla">
        Jyoti Prasad Agarwalla
       </a>
       was the first Indian dubbed film, released in Calcutta on 10 March 1935. Till then, all dialogues of all talkies were had to be recorded at locations during the shooting of the film. Through
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Joymoti_(1935_film)" title="Joymoti (1935 film)">
         Joymoti (1935 film)
        </a>
       </i>
       , dubbing technology was successfully introduced to Indian cinema by Assamese filmmaker
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jyoti_Prasad_Agarwalla" title="Jyoti Prasad Agarwalla">
        Jyoti Prasad Agarwalla
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dainik_Asam_Assamese_daily_82-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Dainik_Asam_Assamese_daily-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The 1930s and 1940s were tumultuous times: India was buffeted by the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">
        Great Depression
       </a>
       , World War II, the
       <a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">
        Indian independence movement
       </a>
       , and the violence of the
       <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_India" title="Partition of India">
        Partition
       </a>
       . Most Bollywood films were unabashedly
       <a href="/wiki/Escapism" title="Escapism">
        escapist
       </a>
       , but there were also a number of filmmakers who tackled tough social issues, or used the struggle for Indian independence as a backdrop for their plots.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica2_85-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-britannica2-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1937
       <a href="/wiki/Ardeshir_Irani" title="Ardeshir Irani">
        Ardeshir Irani
       </a>
       , of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Alam_Ara" title="Alam Ara">
         Alam Ara
        </a>
       </i>
       fame, made the first colour film in Hindi,
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kisan_Kanya_(1937_film)" title="Kisan Kanya (1937 film)">
         Kisan Kanya
        </a>
       </i>
       . The next year, he made another colour film, a version of
       <i>
        Mother India
       </i>
       . However, colour did not become a popular feature until the late 1950s. At this time, lavish romantic musicals and melodramas were the staple fare at the cinema.
      </p>
      <p>
       Following
       <a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">
        India's independence
       </a>
       , the period from the late 1940s to the early 1960s is regarded by film historians as the "Golden Age" of Hindi cinema.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Defining key figures during this time included
       <a href="/wiki/Raj_Kapoor" title="Raj Kapoor">
        Raj Kapoor
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Guru_Dutt" title="Guru Dutt">
        Guru Dutt
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gokulsing-18_90-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Gokulsing-18-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Mehboob_Khan" title="Mehboob Khan">
        Mehboob Khan
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Dilip_Kumar" title="Dilip Kumar">
        Dilip Kumar
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quint_94-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-quint-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hindu_95-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-hindu-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The 1970s was when the name "Bollywood" was coined,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-collaco_96-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-collaco-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-khanna_97-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-khanna-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and when the quintessential conventions of commercial Bollywood films were established.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chaudhuri58_98-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Chaudhuri58-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Key to this was the emergence of the
       <a href="/wiki/Masala_film" title="Masala film">
        masala film
       </a>
       genre, which combines elements of multiple genres (
       <a href="/wiki/Action_film" title="Action film">
        action
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Comedy_film" title="Comedy film">
        comedy
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Romance_film" title="Romance film">
        romance
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drama_film" title="Drama film">
        drama
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Melodrama" title="Melodrama">
        melodrama
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Musical_film" title="Musical film">
        musical
       </a>
       ). The masala film was pioneered in the early 1970s by filmmaker
       <a href="/wiki/Nasir_Hussain" title="Nasir Hussain">
        Nasir Hussain
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       along with screenwriter duo
       <a href="/wiki/Salim-Javed" title="Salim-Javed">
        Salim-Javed
       </a>
       , pioneering the Bollywood
       <a href="/wiki/Blockbuster_(entertainment)" title="Blockbuster (entertainment)">
        blockbuster
       </a>
       format.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chaudhuri58_98-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Chaudhuri58-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics">
        Statistics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Film_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Statistics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_industries_by_number_of_film_productions">
        Largest industries by number of film productions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>

        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Film-production-map-2015.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1707" data-file-width="3308" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Film-production-map-2015.jpg/400px-Film-production-map-2015.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Film-production-map-2015.jpg/600px-Film-production-map-2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Film-production-map-2015.jpg/800px-Film-production-map-2015.jpg 2x" width="400"/>
        </a>

      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_markets_by_box_office_revenue">
        Largest markets by box office revenue
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [

        <li id="cite_note-scienceandmediamuseum-78">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^

           <sup>

              a
             </b>

              b

         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation web">

          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=National+Science+and+Media+Museum&amp;rft.atitle=Decoding+the+Bollywood+poster&amp;rft.date=2013-02-28&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.scienceandmediamuseum.org.uk%2Fdecoding-the-bollywood-poster%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFilm+industry">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>

        <li id="cite_note-Akhtar-79">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-Akhtar_79-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation book">
           <a href="/wiki/Javed_Akhtar" title="Javed Akhtar">
            Aḵẖtar, Jāvīd
           </a>
           ; Kabir, Nasreen Munni (2002).
           <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=_JILAQAAMAAJ" rel="nofollow">
            <i>
             Talking Films: Conversations on Hindi Cinema with Javed Akhtar
            </i>
           </a>
           .
           <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University_Press" title="Oxford University Press">
            Oxford University Press
           </a>
           . p. 49.
           <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
            ISBN
           </a>
           <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780195664621" title="Special:BookSources/9780195664621">
            9780195664621
           </a>
           .
           <q>
            JA: I write dialogue in Urdu, but the action and descriptions are in English. Then an assistant transcribes the Urdu dialogue into
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Devnagari" title="Devnagari">
             Devnagari
            </a>
            because most people read Hindi. But I write in Urdu. Not only me, I think most of the writers working in this so-called Hindi cinema write in Urdu:
            <a href="/wiki/Gulzar" title="Gulzar">
             Gulzar
            </a>
            , or
            <a href="/wiki/Rajinder_Singh_Bedi" title="Rajinder Singh Bedi">
             Rajinder Singh Bedi
            </a>
            or
            <a href="/wiki/Inder_Raj_Anand" title="Inder Raj Anand">
             Inder Raj Anand
            </a>
            or
            <a href="/wiki/Rahi_Masoom_Raza" title="Rahi Masoom Raza">
             Rahi Masoom Raza
            </a>
            or
            <a href="/wiki/Wajahat_Mirza" title="Wajahat Mirza">
             Vahajat Mirza
            </a>
            , who wrote dialogue for films like
            <i>
             <a href="/wiki/Mughal-e-Azam" title="Mughal-e-Azam">
              Mughal-e-Azam
             </a>
            </i>
            and
            <i>
             <a href="/wiki/Gunga_Jumna" title="Gunga Jumna">
              Gunga Jumna
             </a>
            </i>
            and
            <i>
             <a href="/wiki/Mother_India" title="Mother India">
              Mother India
             </a>
            </i>
            . So most dialogue-writers and most song-writers are from the Urdu discipline, even today.
           </q>
          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Talking+Films%3A+Conversations+on+Hindi+Cinema+with+Javed+Akhtar&amp;rft.pages=49&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft.date=2002&amp;rft.isbn=9780195664621&amp;rft.aulast=A%E1%B8%B5%E1%BA%96tar&amp;rft.aufirst=J%C4%81v%C4%ABd&amp;rft.au=Kabir%2C+Nasreen+Munni&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D_JILAQAAMAAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFilm+industry">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-film-world-80">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-film-world_80-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation journal">
           <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=sHlTAAAAYAAJ" rel="nofollow">
            "Film World"
           </a>
           .
           <i>
            Film World
           </i>
           . T.M. Ramachandran.
           <b>
            10
           </b>
           : 65. 1974.
           <q>
            I feel that the Government should eradicate the age-old evil of certifying Urdu films as Hindi ones. It is a known fact that Urdu has been willingly accepted and used by the film industry. Two eminent Urdu writers
            <a href="/wiki/Krishan_Chander" title="Krishan Chander">
             Krishan Chander
            </a>
            and
            <a href="/wiki/Ismat_Chughtai" title="Ismat Chughtai">
             Ismat Chughtai
            </a>
            have said that "more than seventy-five per cent of films are made in Urdu." It is a pity that although Urdu is freely used in films, the producers in general mention the language of the film as "Hindi" in the application forms supplied by the Censor Board. It is a gross misrepresentation and unjust to the people who love Urdu.
           </q>
          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Film+World&amp;rft.atitle=Film+World&amp;rft.volume=10&amp;rft.pages=65&amp;rft.date=1974&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DsHlTAAAAYAAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFilm+industry">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
